Appendix A.9  
Interview: Social- & Boligstyrrelsen 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:165==
Social & Boligstyrelsen 
Page 1 af 1 
Interview Social and Housing Agency on 8/3-2023 
With Tine Faarup - Chief Consultant at the Center for Construction: Sustainability, Health and Energy at 
the Social & Boligstyrelsen 
-Interview conducted by Anders Rafn in relation to Master Thesis at DTU 
 
Social & Boligstyrelsen has initiated some efforts on recycling. 
Promoting the recycling of building materials is part of the National Strategy for Sustainability Initiative 10: 
Safe and Healthy Recycling in Construction. Here, for example, the board focuses on good examples of how 
the properties of recycled building goods can be documented through a number of best practice cases. There 
will also be a focus on concrete reuse, but not specifically recycling of HCS. An analysis of design for separation 
must also be carried out as part of the effort, but it has not yet been initiated. The National Strategy for 
Sustainable Construction is a broad political agreement concluded in March 2021, and it sets the direction for 
the development of sustainable construction in the years to come. 
 
In the political agreement for sustainable construction, which was agreed in May 2021, there is an initiative 
to promote the recycling of load -bearing constructions that have been launched and concluded this year. 
In the project, building types are mapped for different periods, which contain the greatest potential for 
recycling of load -bearing structures based on the parameter’s total economy, safety, health, environment 
and climate. The project will result in a guide to building owners and engineers to support the building 
owner's development towards circular economy. 
 
Buildings with recycled products must meet the same safety and health requirements in City Legislations as 
other buildings. It is the builder who is responsible for the existence of documentation of the properties of 
the construction goods and that they comply with requirements. 
 
The board is aware of the work that takes place in Norway with the reuse of HCS, they are also monitoring 
the work from projects as Precast, BusinessReuse and StructuralReuse.

Appendix A.10  
Interview: Danish Standard 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:167==
Dansk Standard 
Page 1 af 1 
Interview Dansk Standard on 17/2-2023  
With Charlotte Vartou Forsingdal - Senior Consultant 
-Interview conducted by Anders Rafn in relation to Master Thesis at DTU 
 
In connection with the project called "Structural Resuse" at DTU, Dansk Standard has an intention to develop 
national pre-standards. These standards hope to contribute to the greater dissemination of the recycling of 
building components and thus ultimately contribute to a more sustainability future by achieving a more 
circular economy in the construction industry in Denmark. 
 
The project examines whether it is possible, by non-destructive testing (NDT), to reach a method precise and 
effective enough to CE-mark the properties of the reused concrete element. The CE-mark assures us that 
reused products have the same quality as new products. 
 
It is unclear so far whether these pre-standards will affect concrete elements in general or specifically HCS or 
the like. It depends on the results of DTU's studies.  
 
The pre-standards are publicly available. If there is support for it from the European Commission and from 
the other Member States in the CEN, the pre-standards can be used to either develop standards for CE 
marking of recycled building components or revise existing product standards. 
 
Dansk Standard estimates that there are two major challenges in scaling up the recycling of concrete 
elements. On the one hand, new circular business models must be established. Secondly a solution must be 
found for distribution of responsibilities, as the models of linear economy cannot be used immediately 
 
Dansk Standard is a neutral party and is tasked with helping Danish companies get influence on European. 
and international- standards. DS, as a stakeholder in the circular business with reuse of elements, they have 
great interest, and have medium -sized influence over the reuse of building components. This is because DS 
will publish pre -standards as a possible solution for documenting the product properties of recycled building 
components.  
==PAGE:168==
 
 
 
 
 
Appendix A.11  
Interview: Danish Technological Institute 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:169==
Danish Technological Institute 
Page 1 af 1 
Interview Teknologisk Institut on 21/2-2023  
With Katja Udbye Christensen - Business Manager at the Danish Technological Institute 
-Interview conducted by Anders Rafn in relation to Master Thesis at DTU 
 
Katja works at the Danish Technological Institute on a project, where they will make specific proposals for 
Danish requirements for testing and documenting reused HCS. There are currently in Denmark no 
requirements or paradigms for how reused concrete elements should be taken down from existing 
construction or how the properties should be documented and declared. This means that the developer has 
to seek exemption from the legislation if reused concrete elements are to be used in a new building, while 
the developer also accepts increased responsibility for the safety and quality of the building. 
 
The project focuses on reusing HCS, walls and TTs. They also touch the other element types, but only go into 
detail with the three mentioned. It is to define the project a little. In this project, they do not focus on design 
for separation. But this is something that the Danish Technological Institute would like to look into, while at 
the same time being aware that it is not necessarily possible to make collections that are reversible for all 
uses. 
 
When a concrete element is produced, the calculations are not actually made by the consulting engineers, 
but by the manufacturer. The element manufacturers have a spreadsheet used for it. It would probably be 
something in the same style that you can do for reused HCS. Here, however, one would have to do some tests 
on the elements to determine input properties such as concrete compressive strength. There are some 
properties needed for calculations that can be difficult or extensive to test on the reused decks. Here you can 
either choose to perform a test (if possible), choose some conservative values or check the calculations with 
a full -scale test. 
 
HCS’s will often be used in passive environmental impact, where there are no large degradation mechanisms 
that can shorten the life of the concrete. So, if the elements are in good condition and they are handled 
properly doing removal, storage, transport and installation, then it must be assumed that the lifespan is still 
long. 
 
The Danish Technological Institute is still working on the removal methods. It is unclear if they hit the perfectly 
optimal method yet. If the slabs are cast with the wall in the vertical layer/ends, their experience so far shows 
that one has to cut that part free before removal. It may also be necessary to cut a little in the length of the 
HCS to adapt them for new projects. Concrete is cut using a diamond saw. 
It is not quite possible to answer yet whether it is cheaper to reuse HCS than to buy new ones. There is also 
a risk that it may become expensive. But it will also depend on how the prices for new materials develop 
going forward. 
==PAGE:170==
 
 
 
 
 
Appendix A.12  
Interview: Technical University of Denmark 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:171==
Technical University of Denmark 
Page 1 of 2 
 
Interview DTU on 06/3-2023  
With Kristoffer Negendahl - Associate Professor in Department of Civil and Mechanical Engineering DTU 
With Ph.D In Sustainable 
-Interview conducted by Anders Rafn in relation to Master Thesis at DTU. 
 
Kristoffer is working on a project with BIG, GXN and Henning Larsen, where he explores the possibilities of 
flexible construction, and he is involved in preparing a method of examining the strength and quality of 
reused elements in connection with CE marking. The project aims to rethink the industry and the building 
traditions by increasing the flexibility of a building, here you will have the opportunity to replace parts of the 
building or change the purpose of the building. 
He examines the needs of different building parts, as well as how to mathematically assess a flexibility scale 
e.g. [1-6] within some index. For the structural parts, the requirements of cargo, sound, fire and thermal 
properties are investigated, among other things. Here it is also examined whether it makes sense to calculate 
some parts for larger loads than necessary so that they can be transformed later. 
Kristoffer believes that it should be possible to measure in the future with numeric data on the degree of 
flexibility a product has. In addition, one must also find agreement on what this scale should be measured 
against. 
It is important to look ahead. Not looking at how existing buildings can be dismantled now, but how to design 
a building so that you, for example. In the event of a minor intervention, it has the option of adding, removing 
or moving individual structural parts of the building. 
 
A major challenge is who is rewarded by incorporating design for separation? Is it the builder who erects the 
building or the next owner or contractor? This may become necessary to incorporate into the legislation that 
if one builder wants to reduce their CO2 print by incorporating DFD, then the building must be reused to 
some min. % degree. This could be done by categorizing the building in the city plans, saying it must be reused 
to the min. % degree. An alternative could also be to increase the life of the building, since the elements have 
a much greater opportunity to be recycled. 
 
In the same context, is it relevant to assess who is affected by design for separation? When designing the 
HCS for separation by e.g. To change the grout and reinforcement principles, the life of the HCS is extended, 
but on the basis that you change another product. 
 
In the design phase, one must also assess what need the building has and how great an impact it has to 
incorporate a recycling project. 
 
 
==PAGE:172==
Technical University of Denmark 
Page 2 of 2 
 
In connection with design for reuse, one must consider and assess different separation methods. There must 
be different methods as you need competition in the market to make it real, the different contractors have 
different wishes for the separation method. In addition, one can compare the methods of how many steps 
in the process they require, as well as how intact HCS’s are by different methods. 
 
One of the major challenges is to create a widespread standard for CE marking of reused concrete elements. 
Here are different considerations. Should you choose a comprehensive method that requires many 
destructive tests, but has a high precision or should you choose a lesser degree of control and increase 
security and thus create more waste by false positive? Kristoffer helps to perform a cost/benefit analysis on 
the EPD by the different methods. 
One thought for this could be to allow both solutions to be possible, so it is up to the individual contractor to 
choose the solution and thus increase the opportunities and competition in the market. 
==PAGE:173==
 
 
 
 
 
Appendix A.13  
IDA Conference 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:174==
IDA Conference 
Page 1 of 3 
 
Summary of Conference "Direct Reuse of Concrete Ele-
ments" at IDA, Copenhagen V. Tuesday, April 11, 2023 
 
1.1 
Introduction  
 
Our group attended a conference on reused precast hollow core decks at IDA to gain valuable insights 
for our master thesis. The conference focused on the challenge of recycling concrete elements from 
existing construction in new construction and presented the status and concrete results of several Danish 
development projects dealing with this challenge. The conference provided a platform for exchanging 
ideas and experiences among industry professionals, researchers, and students in the field of sustainable 
construction practices. 
The following sections presents a resume of each presentation at the conference.  
1.2 
Structural Reuse, Lisbeth Ottosen  
 
The conference was organized by DTU Sustain and DTU Construct in collaboration with other partici-
pants, including Lendager Group, Aarhus School of Architecture, List Byg, Rambøll, Danish Standard, 
and Gate 21. The presentations focused on three main topics related to the reuse of structural elements. 
Firstly, the presentation discussed the importance of documentation for the reuse of concrete elements 
in construction. It covered what needs to be documented, how to document it in relation to requirements, 
and how to implement these documentation practices in the industry. 
Secondly, non-destructive test methods for concrete elements were reviewed, with 19 different methods 
identified in the market. The most commonly used method was Ultrasonic, which has already been used 
for bridge inspection. The non-destructive methods provide output related to mechanical properties, 
identification of any heterogeneities in the concrete, and the status of the reinforcing steel. 
Lastly, the conference covered different tests of drill cores from existing buildings. 
Overall, the conference aimed to promote sustainable construction practices by highlighting the im-
portance of documentation and non-destructive testing in the reuse of structural elements. The discus-
sion also explored ways to implement these practices in the construction industry. 
 
1.3 
Possibilities for reuse of concrete elements, Katja Udbye 
Christensen  
 
The discussion highlights several reasons why reuse is relevant, including reducing waste and CO2 
emissions, conserving resources, and promoting longevity. However, the speakers also acknowledge 
that the complex nature of reuse poses challenges, particularly in terms of the entire value chain, lack 
of standard solutions, and inadequate legislation to support reuse. 
The conference explores various aspects of reuse, including existing buildings, demolition and han-
dling, cleaning, cutting, and preparing built-in elements, customization, and documentation. The speak-
ers also discuss the design of new buildings using recycled concrete elements, sales/purchases of items, 
==PAGE:175==
IDA Conference 
Page 2 of 3 
 
timing, and requirements. They note that legislation currently does not support direct recycling of con-
crete elements, and there is a need to determine responsibility and recognize the environmental impact 
of such reuse in LCA calculations. 
Overall, the conference emphasizes the importance of finding practical and sustainable solutions to 
promote reuse in the construction industry, despite the challenges it poses. 
 
1.4 
(P)Recast x Søndergaard, Annette Beedholm Rasmussen 
& Søndergaard  
 
In the conference, Søndergaard, a demolition company, presented their experience. 
The conference focused on a project aimed at reusing fully intact  concrete elements as bearing struc-
tures to reduce CO2 footprint and resource consumption, which is relevant to our master's thesis. The 
project specifically dealt with the demounting of subsidized housing from the 60s, 70s, and 80s, with 
a focus on walls, hollow core slabs, and TT-elements. Søndergaard presented their experience with 
the demounting of a school in Copenhagen built in 1997. Out of the 34 hollow core slabs, 22 were 
successfully demounted, but three were destroyed due to their size. Additionally, out of the 18 wall 
elements, 13 were successfully demounted, but three were destroyed during handling.  
These results highlight the importance of proper planning and the role of grouting in the process of 
demounting existing structures for reuse. They reported that preliminary study of structures is essen-
tial to ensure the success of the demounting process, and that the grouting of precast elements can sig-
nificantly affect the ease of disassembling the structural elements. The steps of the demounting pro-
cess is shown in the figure below: 
 
 
==PAGE:176==
IDA Conference 
Page 3 of 3 
 
1.5 
Joints to reuse of hollow core slabs, Henrik Brøner 
Jørgensen  
 
The conference presented the work of Henrik Brøner Jørgensen, an associate professor at University of 
Southern Denmark, on the development of mechanical joints for recycling hollow-core-slabs. Instead 
of having line supports under the HCS, mechanical joints as point supports at the corners. The primary 
focus was how the load is transferred to the joints and how the HCS is acting along the zone nearby the 
point support. Experimental work was carried out by designing the least favorable setup. This was done 
by analiyzing failure for bending and shear by using yield-line-theory and lastly punching shear. 
The results of the tests provided some upper and lower value boundaries but require further investiga-
tions. Overall, the conference emphasized the importance of developing new joint details for recycling 
HCS in sustainable construction practices.

Appendix B  
Elaboration of placement in stakeholder map 
The appendix is made of the following page(s) 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:178==
Stakeholder map 
Page 1 of 4 
 
Elaboration of placement in stakeholder map  
– By Anders Rafn 
Here is an elaboration on why each stakeholder is placed in either high or low influence and interest: 
 
(1) Nordkranen [Client], (2) Rambøll Norge [Engineer], (3) MOE [Engineer], (4) NCC Management 
[Contractor], (5) Tscherning [Contractor], (6) Boligbeton [Supplier], (7) Hilti [Supplier], (8) NCC Production 
[Craftsmen], (9) Social- & Boligstyrelsen [City Legislation], (10) Danish Standard [Publisher], (11) Danish 
Technological Institute [R&D], (12) DTU [UNI] 
 
Keep in mind that each stakeholder is represented through the specific interviews solely. The 
stakeholder map can vary for each stakeholder depending on the specific company representative of 
the stakeholder. The 12 interviews are elaborated below: 
 
[1] Nordkranen: Client (High Influence, Moderate Interest): 
Nordkranen is placed in the high influence category because they are the initiator and primary 
financier of the project. They have the power to shape the direction of the project and make key 
decisions. However, their interest is categorized as moderate because while sustainability is gaining 
importance, their main priority remains profitability.  
 
 
==PAGE:179==
Stakeholder map 
Page 2 of 4 
 
[2] Rambøll Norge: Engineer (Moderate Influence, Small Interest): 
Rambøll Norway is actually the only engineer found in the literature research to how reused HCSs in 
a project, KA13. Rambøll Norway are placed in the moderate influence category because they have 
the expertise and knowledge to influence the technical aspects of the project. However, their interest 
may not be as active as some other stakeholders’. They are considered passive influencers who will 
incorporate the structural DfD-system if they are paid for it but may not actively seek it out otherwise. 
 
[3] MOE Engineer (Moderate Influence, Moderate Interest): 
MOE (have now changed name to Artelia) holds moderate influence on DfD. However, they mention 
that that the influence is most significant in the early stages of decision-making, typically led by the 
architect. MOE suggests that involving engineers in decisions about systems and materials as early 
as possible would be beneficial. Financial considerations present the biggest risk for MOE as advisors. 
Their profit margins are relatively small compared to revenue, so choices that affect the project's 
economy, even by a few percentage points, can quickly lead to losses. Consequently, MOE tends to 
be somewhat conservative in their approach thus they have moderate interest until reuse of HCSs is 
well established. 
 
[4] NCC Management: Contractors (Moderate Influence, Moderate Interest): 
NCC management as contractors have moderate influence in the stakeholder map. While they can 
play a persuasive role in advocating for more sustainable solutions, their primary responsibility lies 
in executing assigned tasks according to the client's wishes. Their interest is also categorized as 
moderate because they are dependent on the client's requirements and engagement. 
 
[5] Tscherning: Contractor (Moderate/Low Influence, High Interest): 
Tscherning is a contractor working with demolition, thus they hold a high interest in the stakeholder 
map. Their involvement and collaboration are essential in adopting a structural DfD-system, as they 
are directly involved in the construction process and have the potential to influence decision-making 
based on their expertise. Their priorities revolve around delivering quality construction while aligning 
with sustainable objectives as determined by the client and industry regulations. As a contractor 
involved in construction projects, they are responsible for executing assigned tasks according to the 
client's requirements, thus the influence is more tilted towards moderate and low. 
 
[6] Boligbeton (High Influence, High Interest): 
Boligbeton is a manufacturer of HCSs, they hold a high influence in the stakeholder map as they are 
responsible for producing the building components. They have a high interest in the incorporation of 
a structural DfD-system as it directly impacts their market and production. Their involvement and 
collaboration are crucial for the successful implementation of sustainable practices. 
==PAGE:180==
Stakeholder map 
Page 3 of 4 
 
[7] Hilti (Low Influence, Low Interest): 
Hilti is a supplier of tools placed in the low influence and interest category because they primarily 
provide tools and equipment for the construction process. Their influence and interest are low as they 
are mostly unaffected by the choices related to the structural DfD-system. Their involvement is 
limited to providing the necessary tools as per the requirements of the contractors and engineers. 
 
[8] NCC Production (Low Influence, Low Interest): 
NCC Production is representative of craftsmen. They are placed in the low influence and interest 
category because they provide a service and are paid accordingly. They are mostly unaffected by the 
choices related to incorporating a structural DfD-system. While their involvement may not be 
significant, it is still important to communicate any changes or requirements to them to ensure smooth 
project execution. 
 
[9] Social- & boligstyrelsen (High Influence, High Interest): 
Social- & boligstyrelsen is representative of city legislation. They hold a high influence in the 
stakeholder map as they are responsible for setting rules and regulations governing construction 
practices. They have a strong interest in sustainable practices and the incorporation of a structural 
DfD-system to promote environmental goals and meet sustainability targets as they are pressured 
from politicians. Their involvement and support are crucial for driving the green transition in the 
construction industry. 
 
[10] Dansk Standard (Low Influence, High Interest): 
Dansk Standard is a publisher. They have low influence in the stakeholder map as they are primarily 
reliant on information and knowledge from other stakeholders, they publish results rather than 
researching it themselves. Their interest, however, is high as they have a purpose of establishing 
circular solutions. Publishers play a role in creating awareness and promoting sustainable practices, 
but they are not directly involved in the decision-making process. 
 
[11] Danish Technological Institute (Moderate-high Influence, High Interest): 
Danish Technological Institute is acting as R&D. They hold a moderate-high influence in the 
stakeholder map. They are involved in a project that focuses on testing and documenting reused 
HCSs. Their interest is high as they are actively engaged in researching and proposing Danish 
requirements for testing and documentation. Their involvement contributes to developing guidelines 
and standards for incorporating recycled building components. 
 
 
==PAGE:181==
Stakeholder map 
Page 4 of 4 
 
[12] DTU (High influence, high interest) 
Kristoffer from DTU working with sustainability demonstrates both high interest and high influence 
in integrating DfD into the construction industry. He is actively engaged in collaborative projects with 
companies trying to explore the potential of flexible construction and evaluates the strength and 
quality of reused elements. The research plays a significant role in shaping decision-making 
processes, influencing industry practices, and contributing to the development of sustainable 
construction methodologies.

Side 1/2
Anvendelsesområde
Weber cementpuds C 100/400 0-2 mm anvendes til pudseopgaver, hvor der stilles skærpede krav til pudslagets robusthed, herunder til repara-
tionsopgaver på sokler, kælderydervægge, betontrapper og betonsokler. Ud fra opgavens beliggenhed, miljøpåvirkninger og krav til holdbarhed 
skal underlaget forbehandles og pudslagets opbygning vurderes i hvert enkelt tilfælde. Der henvises til Weber håndbogen, SBI-anvisning 64, 
Murerhåndbogen (MURO) og anden branche­lit­teratur.
Produktbeskrivelse
Weber cementpuds C 100/400 0-2 mm er en fabriksfremstillet tørmørtel bestående af portland­ce­ment, plastificerende og vedhæftningsforbe-
drende tilsætningsstof samt 0-2 mm ovntørret sand. Tørmørtlen skal kun tilsættes vand før brug. 
 
Produktet er fremstillet på basis af chromatneutraliseret cement. Indholdet af vandopløseligt chromat er mindre end svarende til 2 mg pr. kg 
tør cement. Neutraliseringens holdbarhed svarer til oplysning i HurtigGuiden.
Produktegenskaber
Primære egenskaber 
Mørteltype: Cementmørtel 
Blandingsforhold: C 100/400 
 
Supplerende oplysninger 
 Vandtilsætning: 10-12,5 % (svarer til 2,5-3,1 liter pr. 25 kg tørmørtel) 
Brugstid efter blanding (ved 20 °C): 60 minutter 
Forbrug (ekskl. spild): Typisk ca. 2 kg/m² pr. mm lagtykkelse
Emballage
Varenr.
• xxx2052
DB-nr.
• 5157799
Opbevaring
Holdbarhed: 12 måneder fra produktionsdato 
Opbevaring: Tørt og uåbnet, hævet fra underlaget på paller. Tåler frost.
Blanding
Bland cementpudsen i tvangsblander. Tilsæt vand til ønsket pudsekonsistens svarende til ca. 10 vægt-%. Bland i mindst 10 minutter, indtil 
homogen blanding opnås og bland ikke mere mørtel, end der kan anvendes inden for 60 minutter. Genoprøring kan foretages uden tilsætning 
af vand.

==PAGE:186==
Udførelse
Forarbejde 
Stærkt sugende underlag skal forvandes grundigt – helst dagen forinden. 
 
Pudsning 
 Kast mørtlen på med pudseske eller træk mørtlen på underlaget med stål- eller trækkebræt. Afret i stok og lod med kardæsk, retholt og 
loddestok før sammenrivning med trækkebræt, lunkepudser eller rivebræt. 
 
Efterbehandling 
 Senest ved arbejdets ophør - under mørtlens afbinding og start af hærdning - skal der afdæk­kes effektivt mod nedbør og frost. I tørre perioder 
(varme, blæst) skal pudslaget beskyt­tes mod for hurtig udtørring og eventuelt eftervandes. Udførlig arbejdsbeskrivelse frem­går af Weber 
håndbogen, SBI-anvisning 64, Murerhåndbogen (MURO) og anden branche­lit­teratur.
Anvendelsesbegrænsninger
Færdigblandet mørtel skal senest anvendes inden for 60 minutter. Der må ikke blandes fry­sepunktssænkende midler eller andre tilsætnings-
stoffer i mørtlen. Når blanding af mørtlen er afslut­tet, må der ikke senere iblandes bindemidler, tilslagsmaterialer eller vand. Temperaturen 
under udførelsen skal være over 5 °C - også i underlaget. Lagtykkelser over 8 mm pr. arbejdsgang medfører risiko for dårlig vedhæftning samt 
svind- og skridrevner.
EHS
Saint-Gobain Weber A/S er en kvalitets- og miljøbevidst virksomhed, certificeret i henhold til DS/EN ISO 14001 og DS/EN ISO 9001:2000 af 
Bureau Veritas Certification Denmark A/S. 
 
Fremstillingsprocesser og miljøforhold bliver styret i henhold til godkendte og dokumenterede forretningsgange og instruktioner. Styringen 
gør, at vi altid kan garantere produkter af ensartet, høj kvalitet. Produkterne gennemgår som en del af certificeringen løbende inspektioner og 
afprøvninger.

Blanding
Mørtlen blandes i tvangs- eller horisontalblander. Tilsæt vand til ønsket murekonsistens - normalt svarende til ca. 16 vægt-%. Blandetiden i 
tvangsblander er 5-8 minutter. I horisontalblander afhænger blandetiden af blanderens kapacitet. Vandtilsætningen på horisontalblander 
justeres på flowmeter, indtil ønsket konsistens er opnået. Bland ikke mere mørtel, end der kan anvendes inden for ca. 60 minutter. Mørtlen kan 
genoprøres – dog uden yderligere tilsætning af vand. Som vinterforanstaltning kan op til 60 °C varmt blandevand anvendes.
Udførelse
Forarbejde
Benyt traditionelt murerværktøj.
Opmuring
Mur med fyldte fuger og alligevel så rent, at afrensning kan undgås. Tryk fugerne, når mørtlen er tilpas afbundet. Kost murværket diagonalt for 
at fjerne eventuelle mørtelrester. Fugerne kan i stedet færdiggøres ved traditionel udkradsning (dybde min. 13 mm) og efterfølgende fugning.
Efterbehandling
Afdæk murværket effektivt mod nedbør og frost. Det skal ske senest ved arbejdets ophør, mens mørtlen afbinder og begynder hærdning. Se 
Murerhåndbogen (MURO), SBI-anvisning 64 og diverse pjecer fra Vinterkonsulenterne for Bygge og Anlæg (Teknologisk Institut) samt „Afdæk-
ning af murværk og materialer“ (BYGITEGL.DK). Se vejledning på www.weber.dk.
Anvendelsesbegrænsninger
Færdigblandet mørtel skal anvendes inden for 60 minutter. Frysepunktssænkende midler eller andre tilsætningsstoffer må ikke tilsættes. Når 
mørtlen er færdigblandet, må der ikke senere tilsættes bindemidler, tilslagsmaterialer eller vand.

Veritas Certification Denmark A/S.
Fremstillingsprocesser og miljøforhold bliver styret i henhold til godkendte og dokumenterede forretningsgange og instruktioner. Styringen 
gør, at vi altid kan garantere produkter af ensartet, høj kvalitet. Produkterne gennemgår som en del af certificeringen løbende inspektioner og

18 kg sæk 
Bigbags a 1500 kg 
Bulk
weber Muremørtel KC 35/65/650 Bakke 0-4 mm
PRODUKTBLAD
09.08.2018 
• Færdigblandet mørtel
• Klar til brug
• Tilsæt kun vand
==PAGE:190==
Receptnr.: xxx1008
DB-nr.: 1549442 (sæk)
PR-nr.: 1288537
 
Blanding
Mørtlen blandes i tvangs- eller horisontalblander. Tilsæt vand til ønsket murekonsistens - normalt svarende til ca. 16 vægt-%. Blandetiden i 
tvangsblander er 5-8 minutter. I horisontalblander afhænger blandetiden af blanderens kapacitet. Vandtilsætningen på horisontalblander 
justeres på flowmeter indtil ønsket konsistens er opnået. Bland ikke mere mørtel, end der kan anvendes inden for ca. 60 minutter. Mørtlen kan 
genoprøres – dog uden yderligere tilsætning af vand. Som vinterforanstaltning kan op til 60 °C varmt blandevand anvendes.
Udførelse
Forarbejde
Benyt traditionelt murerværktøj. Teglsten skal være rene og tørre.
Opmuring
Mur med fyldte fuger og alligevel så rent, at afrensning kan undgås. Tryk fugerne, når mørtlen er tilpas afbundet. Kost murværket diagonalt for 
at fjerne eventuelle mørtelrester. Fugerne kan i stedet færdiggøres ved traditionel udkradsning (dybde min. 13 mm) og efterfølgende fugning.
Efterbehandling
Afdæk murværket effektivt mod nedbør og frost. Det skal ske senest ved arbejdets ophør, mens mørtlen afbinder og begynder hærdning. Se 
Murerhåndbogen (MURO), SBI-anvisning 64 og diverse pjecer fra Vinterkonsulenterne for Bygge og Anlæg (Teknologisk Institut) samt „Afdæk-
ning af murværk og materialer“ (BYGITEGL.DK). Se vejledning på www.weber.dk.
Anvendelsesbegrænsninger
Færdigblandet mørtel skal anvendes inden for 60 minutter. Frysepunktssænkende midler eller andre tilsætningsstoffer må ikke tilsættes. Når 
mørtlen er færdigblandet, må der ikke senere tilsættes bindemidler, tilslagsmaterialer eller vand.
EHS
Saint-Gobain Weber er en kvalitets- og miljøbevidst virksomhed, certificeret i henhold til DS/EN ISO 14001 og DS/EN ISO 9001:2015 af Bureau 
Veritas Certification Denmark A/S.
Fremstillingsprocesser og miljøforhold bliver styret i henhold til godkendte og dokumenterede forretningsgange og instruktioner. Styringen 
gør, at vi altid kan garantere produkter af ensartet, høj kvalitet. Produkterne gennemgår som en del af certificeringen løbende inspektioner og 
afprøvninger.
